This is 100% THE BEST Burrito shop in the Bay Area.  I've gone here many times and also try places in the city and these guys are it!
The prices are always reasonable an the burritos are consistently great, they pack'em with a variety of ingredients to balance out the perfect flavor and the veggies in the food are the freshest I've ever had. You can get a killer good sized burrito for $7-$8 and unlike mexican places in the city that charge $10 a burrito and just talk a big game, these guys actually deliver. FYI get the honey chipotle or cajun chicken burrito, and add cheddar, its a bit more but totally worth it!

<rate>4<//rate><Review>Came here once awhile when I crave for dim sum as this place is nearby my in-law house. Waiting time is between 30 - 45 minutes for party of 2 to 4 on Sunday if arrive after 12:00 PM. The restaurant has more family tables than small tables. No space to wait inside. If you have big family & would like to dine here during rainy season, call to reserve a table. My review is only for dim sum as I never dined here for dinner & lunch. Shiu mai, shrimp dumping, steamed beef ball, steamed egg yolk bun, chicken feet are my favorite. The flavor of those dishes were still the same when I ate here today except steamed egg yolk bun. I didn't see the running egg yolk when I broke it in half & not moist. Bit of disappointed. I always ordered egg yolk bun when I ate here. First time ordered taro puff & beef organ in daikon. Love both dishes. Taro puffs weren't oily & decent amount of minced pork inside with taste of taro. Beef organs were soft & flavorful. Overall, great customer services & foods with affordable price. Parking is easy as the restaurant locates in the residential area. < Review>
Great location, clean and comfortable.  The shower could be an issue for some.  Water was not super hot ever. The pictures online are slightly deceptive.  This place is not nearly as cute as it is in the pictures.  It is adequate, clean and walkable if you are in good shape. But, for the price you may find better lodging. Also, the lobby is closed, no cleaning service, no coffee, limited staff if you want anything....all supposedly COVID related, but still we stayed at our hotels on this trip without these restrictions.  The hot tub is closed.  Patio area is small and slightly dated.< /Review>

<name>Tyger Woods< /name><date>1618012291246< /date><Rating>1< /Rating>< Text>
Small rooms, thin walls, horrible service. Stayed in Carmel for 8 days at three different hotels. This was hands down one of the worst hotel experiences we had that week if not throughout the past decade while visiting Carmel. We stayed at the sister hotel Playa de Carmel (which was great) and decided to visit Hotel Carmel to enjoy the hot tub and outdoor fireplace. On arrival we went to inspect the amenities only to find an empty spa and firepit/fireplace that the staff refused to turn on for us even though we saw another couple enjoying it a few minutes earlier. When booking the hotel the front desk was glad to mention the hot tub but failed to include details of it's inoperability due to Covid-19. Once checked in to the room, we were disappointed at the lack of space and super cramped bathroom not to mention paper thin walls. After 1 night, we decided to cut our 3 night stay short and booked a room @ Svengaards across the street. While not as 'nice' it had ample room and friendlier service. As we were packing up ready to leave, the staff were loudly conversing about how happy they were to have our room check out. Super unprofessional especially when we apologized for the early check out and personally tipped the lady @ the front desk $100. AVOID. Difficult to mess up a hotel stay in Carmel but this one managed to pull it off!< /Text>

This is essentially a motel, charging luxury hotel prices. For over $400 per night, they provided a basic room overlooking the parking lot. Shockingly, the hotel does not even have air conditioning, unheard of for even the lowest budget lodging, and something they don‚Äôt tell you on that snazzy website of theirs or when you make a reservation. To make matters worse, the windows are very old, with non functioning cranks that prevent you from opening and closing them. When we complained about how uncomfortable the room was, we were simply told that the windows were very old and needed replacing (no kidding). Breakfast consisted of a tray of bagels and some yogurt cartons. As others have noted, they tack on a resort fee to the already high published price, despite the fact that this is not disclosed in advance, and there are no resort amenities to speak of. In many years of traveling, I‚Äôve never received so little value for my money.<//Text>

Ive been to a lot of theindian  restaurants around here in Bakersfield and although a lot of them are great, they don't really have a "street food" type menu.

<Text>If you are in Bakersfield and craving some authentic Indian food then Punjabi Dhaba is a must try. It's a small place which can seat around 35 to 40 people, with limited menu but really cheap and amazing and authentic punjabi food.
We tried Dal Makhani, Chole masala and Chicken Tikka Masala with Laccha Paratha and Buttered Roti. Dal Makhani and Chole Masala tasted exactly like what you will have back in northern parts of India. Chicken Tikka masala was also creamy and mildly spicy and tasted great. Service was very quick and the uncle at Cash Counter was super nice too. Overall great experience and food.
NOTE: THIS PLACE ACCEPTS CASH ONLY.< /Text><rating>5< /rating><gmap_id>0x80ea6adf271e4d87:0x270e1f4d6d0e9f50</gmap_id><Resp>None<//Resp></record>

< rating>

< text>
The food is great. Rich, spicy, and well-made with thoroughness. Not your quickly slapped together slop.
The set up is two food cart trucks, and you order thru the window of one.
There is covered seating, which is open, but there is a heater for those cold days.
The rotis are big, the parantha is good. The curries are good.
The people are the best. The person who seemed like he owned the place talked to us about how the place got reviewed in the NY times and how they sometimes run out of curries late at night on a few days. Genuine people, genuine Punjabi food.< /text>

Amazing and comforting Punjabi good right in the middle of Bakersfield, complete dhaba style. Very warm people running the show here and if there is anything that trumps their food, then it's their courteousness. Service is quick and they only accept cash. Try their lachcha paratha without fail. You can thank me later.</Text>

<date>1573454950438<//date><rating>1<//rating>< Text>
went here after reading many reviews on another site. I recently moved here, the reason I read so many reviews. they claimed that the food was " the bomb ",  "taste home cooked" or "great food"  So when I arrived the outdoor seating was covered in  dirt. in a  farming  community a place with outside seating should  have someone at the very least be rinsing the table tops off where people eat,
The menu was very very limited & was printed on a tattered piece of plastic with something written by hand on it that was too smudged to read & taped to the ledge where you place your order.
I have been eating indian food for about 47 years now from all over L.A. and the San Fernando valley. so I think im a pretty good judge of indian food. Over the years I've had Punjabi home cooking  made by co workers for countless pot lucks or parties  So all i can say to those 5 star reviews  is  WHAT!! and to those looking for good  indian food  look elsewhere  I would rate the food at minus 1  if I could< /Text>

< review>
Would definitely recommend this place to anyone who's craving some Indian food. It's probably the best in Bakersfield!
We were returning from Las Vegas to go back home towards California, and hadn't had our lunch yet; it was 630 pm. We were so hungry and the food of this place just reminded us of home! This place has less parking at the front but don't worry about the location cause the moment we entered the smell was just amazing. We ordered Sahi Paneer, chole, roti and dal makhani with jeera rice. Everything was just absolutely delicious! The best was Sahi Paneer and the roti was like home chapati. The roti was fresh and hot. Even the onions given on the side were good and reminded us of India.< /review>

<UserId.>113650483280090391046< /UserId.><Name>Soniya Ahuja< /Name><time>1555298679662<//time>< Rate>
5</Rate>
< Review>
For a quick stop and super fast service on I5, this is a great spot. The food was delicious. The paneer was just as soft as we would eat at Punjab. The food was home cooked with a lovely lady manning the stove. The menu was quite limited but that is expected of a food truck. However the masala chaas, shahi paneer and Dal Makhani that we had were absolutely yummy and tasted just like the food at a good Punjabi Dhaba at Punjab or Haryana. The paratha was well stuffed, as you'll find at a proper punjabi restaurant back home. Meant to be consumed with salted butter, the taste was one to remember for a street side eatery. Order to table took about 7 minutes. So pretty quick<//Review>

< username>
Carlos Godinez< /username>
< date>
1550652477394<//date>
<rate>5</rate>< Review>
Once I got to this little place I was greeted and welcomed by the owner with full on positive vibes, told me which dishes they had available ;because they dont always serve the same thing here which I dont mind.
I decided to go with the original, Chicken Tikka Masala, sweet but fiery hot because well that's how I wanted it and thats how I got it, keep in mind that your level of spice is all on how you order it, in other words they ask how spicy you want it. The food was given to me in a container so I can gradually serve myself as I went on digging in with their warm Rotti (indian style tortillas). The Chicken Tikka was as good as it smelled, the meat was tender and full of flavor till the last flaming hot bite.
As for my lady, she decided to go with the Chole Masala which she wanted spicy as well. Chole Masala was new to me so I decided to give it a go, it wasnt as spicy as my dish was but was as equally delicious.
I might be wrong but I believe it was a type of curry with chickpeas, cilantro, onion and maybe some ginger to give it that kick. She enjoyed this dish with a big ol Paratha (potatoe stuffed tortilla) which I had to try with me being a potato enthusiast, and I gotta say, I didnt just have one , two or three bites of this, I had to get my own before I finished hers.

Punjabi Dhaba is one of those hidden gems that I came across, now with them being on the map you can also find this place too.
Great food, great people, Cash only.
Enjoy</Review>

<Text>We stopped by on our way up from LA, after unsuccessfully searching for South Indian food along the way. Boy was that a good happenstance!

The place is tiny. It's literally a food truck + some seating. And it's very difficult to see it if you are driving by. We had to look around a little after parking on the street nearby. The signs aren't particular good.

The menu is pretty short, which is surprising for an Indian restaurant. The girlfriend had a ton of questions about what the various dishes were, which the owner dude explained pretty well. We got a chai (oh definitely try it), a 16oz order of butter chicken (which is actually a lot, we later realized), an 8oz serving of the sabzi (mixed vegetables dish), and a lot of roti.

The butter chicken was some of the best I've ever had. You have the option to get it mild/medium/hot BTW. Be careful with the hot. It definitely is spicy.
The mixed vegetables dish was really good too, but the chicken totally took over my taste buds. I had to buy an extra order to go üò¨.
Roti were really good too. They use butter to dab the insides, which makes it extra yummy.

Overall, couldn't find a negative with the food. It's extremely bare bones, so go just did the food.</Text>< pictures>
None< /pictures>

I live in Sacramento area and there are no dealers here who offer in-home demos of gear. I was looking for information on a particular dac and found Alma's contact info listed on the dac manufacturer's website. I called just to ask questions. Alex was incredibly patient and helpful.
